Rowling cleared this up in a later interview by stating that she had decided that she did not want Hermione to share a middle name with <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Umbridge" title="Dolores Umbridge">Professor Umbridge</a>, and thus changed it to Jean, which is a female variant of the name John, meaning "God is gracious."<sup id="cite_ref-Jean_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jean-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granger_(name)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Granger (name)">Granger</a> is another word for farmer; specifically, it was the title of a farm bailiff, who oversaw the collection of rent and taxes from the barns of a feudal lord. It is a surname of English and French origin, derived from the Anglo-Norman <i>grainger</i> and the French <i>grangier</i>, both of which come from Latin <i>granica</i>, meaning "granary." It recalls Hermione's <a href="/wiki/Non-magic_people" title="Non-magic people">Muggle</a> roots. Her original last name was "Puckle," but Rowling later decided this didn't suit her character.
</p><p>Hermione may be named after <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clive_Granger" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Clive Granger">Sir Clive Granger</a>, a Nobel Prize-winning British economist who taught in Britain at the University of Nottingham and described the "<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granger_causality" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Granger causality">Granger causality</a>." Or possibly after Granger, one of the society of people who memorised books in <i>Fahrenheit 451</i>.
</p><p>The reason of choosing such an uncommon name as Hermione for the character is because, according to Rowling, she did not bear getting any child mocked because of sharing a name with an "insufferable know-it-all" such as Hermione.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Behind_the_scenes">Behind the scenes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger?veaction=edit&amp;section=72" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Edit section: Behind the scenes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger?action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Behind the scenes"><svg class="wds-icon wds-icon-tiny section-edit-pencil-icon"><use xlink:href="#wds-icons-pencil-tiny"></use></svg>edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Hermione's appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i></p> 		 	</figcaption> </figure>
<ul><li><figure class="thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 152px"> 	<a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f6/Hermione_pottermore.PNG/revision/latest?cb=20200824155217" class="image"><img alt="" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" decoding="async" width="150" height="186" class="thumbimage lazyload" data-image-name="Hermione pottermore.PNG" data-image-key="Hermione_pottermore.PNG" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f6/Hermione_pottermore.PNG/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/150?cb=20200824155217" /></a> 	<noscript><a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f6/Hermione_pottermore.PNG/revision/latest?cb=20200824155217" class="image"><img alt="" src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f6/Hermione_pottermore.PNG/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/150?cb=20200824155217" decoding="async" width="150" height="186" class="thumbimage" data-image-name="Hermione pottermore.PNG" data-image-key="Hermione_pottermore.PNG" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f6/Hermione_pottermore.PNG/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/150?cb=20200824155217" /></a></noscript> 	<figcaption class="thumbcaption"> 		 			<a href="/wiki/File:Hermione_pottermore.PNG" class="info-icon"><svg><use xlink:href="#wds-icons-info-small"></use></svg></a> 		 		 		 			<p class="caption"><a href="/wiki/Wizarding_World_(website)" title="Wizarding World (website)">Wizarding World</a> illustration of Hermione.</p> 		 	</figcaption> </figure>Hermione is portrayed by French-born <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">British</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">film adaptations</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">Goblet of Fire</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Half-Blood Prince</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 1">Deathly Hallows: Part 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 2">Part 2</a></i> and is one of the 14 characters to appear in all 8 film adaptations. Watson also portrayed her in the short <i><a href="/wiki/The_Queen%27s_Handbag" title="The Queen&#39;s Handbag">The Queen's Handbag</a></i>.</li>
<li>Emma Watson actually had to dye her hair darker for the first three films. Emma naturally has light brown hair.
<ul><li>Her hair changes every film, somehow, the cases being:
<ul><li>In the first film, her hair is medium brown, straight, and very bushy.</li>
<li>In the second film, her hair is longer than it ever was in the film series, has grown lighter (caramel brown), and is wavy, not straight.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban"><i>The Prisoner of Azkaban</i></a>, her hair is merely shoulder length and is shown to become curly.</li>
<li>In <i>The Goblet of Fire</i>, her hair has gone a bit bushy again and back to being gently wavy, along with being a lighter brown.</li>
<li>In <i>Order of the Phoenix</i>, Hermione's hair changes yet <i>again</i>: it became almost straight, and its length now reaches just below armpit.</li>
<li>In <i>The Half-Blood Prince</i>, she is seen with a curlier tone  and hair that reaches a few inches above the earlier film.</li>
<li>In the <i>Deathly Hallows</i> films, her hair becomes longer (chest-length) again, but reverts to being straight again, possibly due to the stress of being on the run. Notably, the second film features her hair becoming medium brown again.</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li>Hermione's hair colour in the last five films became lighter due to Emma Watson reverting to her natural hair colour.</li>
<li>As Hermione said in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>, she used to wear braces, presumingly in order to correct her dentition. This was then made unnecessary when she let Madam Pomfrey, while shrinking her teeth elongated by Draco Malfoy's <i><a href="/wiki/Densaugeo" title="Densaugeo">Densaugeo</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hex" title="Hex">hex</a>, "<i>carry on a little bit</i>". According to Hermione, Mr and Mrs Granger wouldn't<i> </i>"<i>be too pleased</i>" by this.</li>
<li>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, Hermione and all her family can ski, although when it comes to her it isn't "<i>really</i> [her] <i>thing</i>".</li>
<li>Hermione is portrayed by British actress <a href="/wiki/Noma_Dumezweni" title="Noma Dumezweni">Noma Dumezweni</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Cursed_Child_(play)#Original_West_End_production" title="Harry Potter and the Cursed Child (play)">original West End production</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Cursed_Child" title="Harry Potter and the Cursed Child">Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cast1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cast1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sophie_Thompson" title="Sophie Thompson">Sophie Thompson</a> plays Hermione when she is disguised as <a href="/wiki/Mafalda_Hopkirk" title="Mafalda Hopkirk">Mafalda Hopkirk</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 1">Deathly Hallows: Part 1</a>, </i>as does <a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a> when she is disguised as <a href="/wiki/Bellatrix_Lestrange" title="Bellatrix Lestrange">Bellatrix Lestrange</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 2">Deathly Hallows: Part 2</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Radcliffe" title="Daniel Radcliffe">Daniel Radcliffe</a> also plays Hermione in the "Seven Potters" scene. However, Emma provided the voice for Hermione while she was in disguise on all three occasions.</li>
<li>Although the novels describe Hermione as having rather large front teeth in her younger years, this is not depicted in the films, as Watson never had large teeth and couldn't speak when applied with bucked teeth.</li>
<li>However, in an on-screen commentary for the Blu-Ray release of <i>Philosopher's Stone</i>, reveals that the final scene of the film <i>does</i> show Hermione's large front teeth. According to Columbus, the scene - which was actually the first to be shot - was filmed with Emma Watson wearing fake teeth to simulate the look of Hermione, but that after filming the sequence it was decided to continue using them would have been impractical. Via edits, the appearance of Hermione's teeth is minimised, but they are still visible when she speaks in the scene.</li>
<li>Also, Hermione's hair is only shown as bushy for the first film. Later, her hair is shown as wavy in the second film, and curly in the third film onwards, although it does briefly take on a bushy appearance for comedic effect during the potion-making contest sequence of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>, the film is the second one featuring Hermione with curly hair, after <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>.</li>
<li>Hermione's <a href="/wiki/Patronus_Charm" title="Patronus Charm">Patronus</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Otter" title="Otter">otter</a>, is Rowling's favourite animal. The otter is in the family <i>Mustelidae</i>, the same as the weasel, although the latter do not live near water.</li></ul>
<p>Hermione’s Patronus, a shining silver otter, was gambolling around her.
</p><p>
‘They are sort of nice, aren’t they?’ she said, looking at it fondly.<br />          <em>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</em></p><figure class="thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 182px"> 	<a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f7/OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20190125011901" class="image"><img alt="" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" decoding="async" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage lazyload" data-image-name="OOTP promo Hermione Granger wand.jpg" data-image-key="OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f7/OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20190125011901" /></a> 	<noscript><a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f7/OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20190125011901" class="image"><img alt="" src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f7/OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20190125011901" decoding="async" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" data-image-name="OOTP promo Hermione Granger wand.jpg" data-image-key="OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/f/f7/OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20190125011901" /></a></noscript> 	<figcaption class="thumbcaption"> 		 			<a href="/wiki/File:OOTP_promo_Hermione_Granger_wand.jpg" class="info-icon"><svg><use xlink:href="#wds-icons-info-small"></use></svg></a> 		 		 		 			<p class="caption">Emma Watson as Hermione Granger in a promotional picture for <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i></p> 		 	</figcaption> </figure>
<ul><li>Hermione is rendered Hermelien in Dutch and Hermine in German. They in turn are similar to the words Hermelijn in Dutch and Hermelin in German, which means Stoat, which is a species of Weasel.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>, Hermione tells <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Scrimgeour" title="Rufus Scrimgeour">Rufus Scrimgeour</a> that she is not planning to pursue career in Magical Law. Ironically, that's where she ends up after leaving Hogwarts, following a stint in the Department for the Regulation and Control of Magical Creatures.</li>
<li>In early drafts, Hermione was supposed to have <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger%27s_sister" title="Hermione Granger&#39;s sister">a Muggle sister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EBF_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBF-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In a 2004 interview with the BBC on World Book Day, J.K. Rowling revealed the following:‘I always planned that Hermione would have a younger sister but she’s never made an appearance and somehow it feels like it might be too late now.’</li>
<li>On several occasions - during their frequent bickering - Hermione is seen calling Ron by his full name to express her annoyance. Some examples include her squabble with Ron about <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pettigrew" title="Peter Pettigrew">Scabbers</a> (<i>"Ronald has lost his rat"</i>), and when they argue about Ron's sister <a href="/wiki/Ginevra_Weasley" title="Ginevra Weasley">Ginny</a> dating <a href="/wiki/Dean_Thomas" title="Dean Thomas">Dean Thomas</a> <i>("Honestly Ronald, they're just holding hands - and snogging"</i>).</li>
<li>Hermione admitted to successfully trying out "a few simple spells" just before her <a href="/wiki/First_year" title="First year">first year</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts_School_of_Witchcraft_and_Wizardry" title="Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry">Hogwarts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PS_3-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> but, in spite of <a href="/wiki/Underage_magic" title="Underage magic">underage magic</a> being banned, she apparently never received a warning from the <a href="/wiki/Improper_Use_of_Magic_Office" title="Improper Use of Magic Office">Improper Use of Magic Office</a> for it. This may be because, since she had not yet attended Hogwarts as an official student, the Ministry overlooked it just as they overlooked when young <a href="/wiki/Tom_Riddle" title="Tom Riddle">Tom Riddle</a> used magic before attending Hogwarts to move objects, help him climb down a steep cliff, etc.; and also as they overlooked when young <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry</a> made the glass of the boa constrictor cage disappear, made his own hair grow back to normal long length after <a href="/wiki/Petunia_Dursley" title="Petunia Dursley">Aunt Petunia</a> cut it, etc. Severus Snape indicated as much to Lily Evans when they were both children about Lily's own use of magic before she was a student.</li>
<li>The screenwriter for the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kloves" title="Steve Kloves">Steve Kloves</a> has said that Hermione is his favourite character, commenting: "There's something about her fierce intellect coupled with a complete lack of understanding of how she affects people sometimes that I just find charming and irresistible to write."<sup id="cite_ref-DVD_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DVD-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, Hermione is shown to be aware of what the term "<a href="/wiki/Mudblood" title="Mudblood">Mudblood</a>" means when <a href="/wiki/Draco_Malfoy" title="Draco Malfoy">Draco Malfoy</a> uses the slur against her, whereas in the novel, she has never heard the word before and Ron explains its meaning to her and Harry.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, Professor Binns calls Hermione "Miss Grant." It is also made known that Binns calls everyone different names, with Binns also calling Harry Potter "Mr Perkins."</li>
<li>Hermione's <a href="/wiki/Boggart" title="Boggart">Boggart</a> in her third year was <a href="/wiki/Minerva_McGonagall" title="Minerva McGonagall">Professor McGonagall</a> telling her that she had "failed everything," which Rowling later commented showed that "underneath Hermione's snootiness there is a lot of insecurity and a great fear of failure."<sup id="cite_ref-JKRHG_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JKRHG-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  Hermione did everything perfectly until she reached the trunk with the Boggart in it. After about a minute inside it, she burst out again, screaming.‘Hermione!’ said Lupin, startled. ‘What’s the matter?’</li></ul>
<p>‘P-P-Professor McGonagall!’ Hermione gasped, pointing into the trunk. ‘Sh-she said I’d failed           everything!’
<em>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</em>
</p>
<ul><li>In the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>, Hermione is shown to be wearing a pink set of dress robes rather than periwinkle blue, as in the novel.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>, Hermione told <a href="/wiki/Horace_Slughorn" title="Horace Slughorn">Slughorn</a> and the Slug Club about her parents being <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentists</a>, but no one, except Harry, knew what dentists were.</li>
<li>Hermione shared a last name with potioneer <a href="/wiki/Hector_Dagworth-Granger" title="Hector Dagworth-Granger">Hector Dagworth-Granger</a>, though she informed <a href="/wiki/Horace_Slughorn" title="Horace Slughorn">Horace Slughorn</a> that she did not think they were related, since she was <a href="/wiki/Muggle-born" title="Muggle-born">Muggle-born</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HBP_23-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBP-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> However, the theory that Muggle-borns have some sort of wizarding ancestry suggests Slughorn might be right about Hermione and Hector being related because every Muggle-born must have had a <a href="/wiki/Squib" title="Squib">Squib</a> ancestor.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry</a> mentions that the only spell Hermione ever had trouble with was the <a href="/wiki/Patronus_Charm" title="Patronus Charm">Patronus Charm</a>, although she was among the first of the D.A. to master the spell and casts it successfully multiple times throughout the series. This may have something to do with the emotional nature of the spell; Harry, due to his inability to cut off his emotions, is particularly adept at this spell, while the logical Hermione has issues with it. It may also have something to do with the caster's self confidence as J.K. Rowling has stated that Hermione is afraid of failure and Harry's first powerful uses of the spell, at a Quidditch match and when he saved Sirius, seem more motivated by his confidence rather then a positive memory.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry,_A_History:_The_True_Story_of_a_Boy_Wizard,_His_Fans,_and_Life_Inside_the_Harry_Potter_Phenomenon" title="Harry, A History: The True Story of a Boy Wizard, His Fans, and Life Inside the Harry Potter Phenomenon">Harry, A History</a></i>, Rowling told <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Anelli" title="Melissa Anelli">Melissa Anelli</a> that Steve Kloves had suspected something might happen between Hermione and Harry while reading <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>: "He felt a certain pull between them at that point. And I think he's right. There are moments when [Harry and Hermione] touch, which are charged moments. One when she touches his hair as he sits on the hilltop reading about Dumbledore and Grindelwald, and [two] the moment when they walk out of the graveyard with their arms around each other. Now the fact is that Hermione shares moments with Harry that Ron will never be able to participate in. He walked out. She shared something very intense with Harry. So I think it could have gone that way."<sup id="cite_ref-HAH_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HAH-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Singer <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katy_B" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Katy B">Katy B</a> auditioned to play Hermione, but was dismissed when the casting director discovered that she had not read the books.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Church" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Charlotte Church">Charlotte Church</a> also auditioned, but was too old for the part.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Watson says that her favourite scene during the film series is the Yule Ball sequence in the fourth film, just like Rupert Grint.</li>
<li>In the Harry Potter books, Hermione has brown hair, but in the films she has more of a light brown.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>, Hermione snaps at Harry when he tells her to give a message to Ron, saying "I'm not an owl." An owl is used for carrying messages, but her name, Hermione, drives from Hermes, the Greek messenger of the gods.</li>
<li>In the same adaptation, the subplot of Hermione standing up for House-Elves rights was left out of the film adaptations entirely.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 1">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 1</a></i>, Hermione is shown leaving her parents house, however this is only ever mentioned in the books.</li>
<li>In the same film, Hermione is shown to be able to play the piano, which she attempts to teach <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Weasley" title="Ronald Weasley">Ron</a> to do while at Grimmauld Place.</li>
<li>In the same adaptation, Bellatrix uses her knife to carve the word "Mudblood" into Hermione's arm during her interrogation. This was not inscribed in the book, but was an idea that Emma Watson came up with, along with Helena Bonham Carter.</li>
<li>Hermione cries in seven of the eight films:
<ul><li>First film: After Ron insulted her by saying she has no friends because she is a nightmare and hides in the girls' bathroom.</li>
<li>Second film: When she, her friends and the other students cheer for Hagrid after he returns to Hogwarts from Azkaban at the end of the film.</li>
<li>Third film: When she, Harry and Ron saw Buckbeak's apparent execution.</li>
<li>Fourth film: After Ron ruined her night at the Yule Ball.</li>
<li>Sixth film: When Ron started having a relationship with Lavender Brown and when Dumbledore died.</li>
<li>Seventh film: When Ron abandoned her and Harry during the Horcrux hunt, and after Bellatrix has interrogated her and carved the word 'Mudblood' on her arm with <a href="/wiki/Bellatrix_Lestrange%27s_knife" title="Bellatrix Lestrange&#39;s knife">her knife</a>.</li>
<li>Eighth film: When she is worried about Harry going into the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_Forest" title="Forbidden Forest">Forbidden Forest</a> to have Voldemort kill him.</li></ul></li>
<li>Hermione's surname was 'Puckle', in early drafts of Harry Potter. It was later changed to Granger.</li>
<li>Initially, J.K. Rowling had stated that Hermione's middle name was "Jane." However, Rowling later changed it to "Jean" after deciding that she did not want Hermione to share a middle name with <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Umbridge" title="Dolores Umbridge">Dolores Umbridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jean_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jean-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Hermione's <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger%27s_wand" title="Hermione Granger&#39;s wand">wand</a> <a href="/wiki/Wand_wood" title="Wand wood">wood</a> of vine corresponds to her <a href="/wiki/19_September" title="19 September">birthday</a> in the Celtic calendar, which Rowling did intentionally as a connection between Hermione's wand, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter%27s_wand" title="Harry Potter&#39;s wand">Harry's wand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Weasley%27s_first_wand" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronald Weasley&#39;s first wand">Ron's wand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In the Celtic calendar, the vine was a symbol of passionate emotions in both extremes—happiness and wrath — and was connected to fulfilling goals and finding balance.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>When asked, Rowling said that if Hermione looked into the <a href="/wiki/Mirror_of_Erised" title="Mirror of Erised">Mirror of Erised</a> in the summer of <a href="/wiki/1997" title="1997">1997</a>, she would have seen herself, Harry, and Ron "alive and unscathed" and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Riddle" title="Tom Riddle">Voldemort</a> defeated, and might also "see herself closely entwined with <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Weasley" title="Ronald Weasley">a special person</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Hermione is a playable character in the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(video_game)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (video game)">video game</a> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_2_(video_game)" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 2 (video game)">adaptations</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>, <i>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</i>, <i>Harry Potter and the Half Blood Prince</i> (only in duel mode), and '<b><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows:_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows: Part 2</a><i>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></b></li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(video_game)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (video game)">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban: The Video Game</a></i> for PC, Peeves refers to Hermione as "Grunge." He always uses the last names for his insulting versions in the games, producing: Potter = Potty, Weasley = Weasel, and Granger = Grunge.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/LEGO_Harry_Potter:_Years_1-4" title="LEGO Harry Potter: Years 1-4">LEGO Harry Potter: Years 1-4</a></i>, Hermione has the ability to control <a href="/wiki/Crookshanks" title="Crookshanks">Crookshanks</a> and translate ancient runes since first year, rather than third year.</li>
<li>A variant of Hermione is available in the "Downloadable Character Pack" <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downloadable_content" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Downloadable content">DLC</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/LEGO_Harry_Potter:_Years_5-7" title="LEGO Harry Potter: Years 5-7">LEGO Harry Potter: Years 5-7</a></i>. The variant is called "Hermione (Pink Dress)" because it portrays Hermione wearing the <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger%27s_dress_robes" title="Hermione Granger&#39;s dress robes">pink dress</a> she wore to the <a href="/wiki/Yule_Ball" title="Yule Ball">Yule Ball</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>.</li>
<li>In the books, several times Ron and Hermione repeat phrases said by one another; for example, when Hermione, in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</a></i>, wanted to produce fire in order to destroy the Devil's Snare, Ron tells her: "Are you a witch or not?" meaning that they could make fire by their wands. During the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hogwarts" title="Battle of Hogwarts">Battle of Hogwarts</a>, Ron expressed regret for not having Crookshanks there to stop the Whomping Willow and Hermione told him, "Are you a wizard or not?" leading Ron to levitate a stick into the tree's weak spot. Furthermore, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Seven_Potters" title="Battle of the Seven Potters">Battle of the Seven Potters</a>, Tonks said Ron was amazing, having defeated many Death Eaters. When Hermione looked surprised, Ron said:"Always that tone of surprise." Hermione says the same thing when Ron told her she was very beautiful, during Bill and Fleur's wedding.</li>
<li>Curiously, Hermione (a Muggle-born witch) is said having passed the Apparition exam and thus having obtained the Licence to Apparate,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> whereas her best friend and future husband, Ron Weasley (a Pureblood wizard), is said having passed the Muggle driving exam, thus having obtained the Muggle driving licence.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="Author's_comments"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Author.27s_comments">Author's comments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger?veaction=edit&amp;section=73" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Edit section: Author&#039;s comments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger?action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Author&#039;s comments"><svg class="wds-icon wds-icon-tiny section-edit-pencil-icon"><use xlink:href="#wds-icons-pencil-tiny"></use></svg>edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 162px"> 	<a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/e/ee/TI4U_u1141962737.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080817135852" class="image"><img alt="" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" decoding="async" width="160" height="200" class="thumbimage lazyload" data-image-name="TI4U u1141962737.jpg" data-image-key="TI4U_u1141962737.jpg" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/e/ee/TI4U_u1141962737.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/160?cb=20080817135852" /></a> 	<noscript><a href="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/e/ee/TI4U_u1141962737.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080817135852" class="image"><img alt="" src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/e/ee/TI4U_u1141962737.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/160?cb=20080817135852" decoding="async" width="160" height="200" class="thumbimage" data-image-name="TI4U u1141962737.jpg" data-image-key="TI4U_u1141962737.jpg" data-src="https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/harrypotter/images/e/ee/TI4U_u1141962737.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/160?cb=20080817135852" /></a></noscript> 	<figcaption class="thumbcaption"> 		 			<a href="/wiki/File:TI4U_u1141962737.jpg" class="info-icon"><svg><use xlink:href="#wds-icons-info-small"></use></svg></a> 		 		 		 			<p class="caption">Hermione Granger in her <a href="/wiki/1992" title="1992">second year</a></p> 		 	</figcaption> </figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a> has said that she loosely based Hermione at the age of eleven on herself at the same age, though an exaggerated version:
</p>
<dl><dd>"<i>...none of the characters in the books are directly taken from life. Real people did inspire a few of them, but of course once they are on the page they become something completely different. But, yeah, Hermione is a caricature of what I was when I was eleven — a real exaggeration, I wasn't that clever — Hermione is a borderline genius at points — and I hope I wasn't that annoying... sometimes she is an incredible know-it-all.</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-WBUR_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBUR-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Rowling has gone on to say that Hermione, Harry, and Ron are all "<i>a bit like different parts of my personality</i>" as well as her favourite characters, along with <a href="/wiki/Rubeus_Hagrid" title="Rubeus Hagrid">Rubeus Hagrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" title="Albus Dumbledore">Albus Dumbledore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Weasley" title="Fred Weasley">Fred</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Weasley" title="George Weasley">George Weasley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luna_Lovegood" title="Luna Lovegood">Luna Lovegood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EBF_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBF-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and that Hermione and Dumbledore were the most useful characters for <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exposition_(literary_technique)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Exposition (literary technique)">exposition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DVD_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DVD-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> She also identified Hermione as "the most brilliant" of her group of friends and confirmed that "<i>Harry needs her badly</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Rowling has also said that she considers Hermione to be "<i>a very strong female character</i>," as well as "<i>the brightest character</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rowling has also stated that, from a feminist point of view, she is very proud of Hermione. In her words, Hermione does not "play the game" in refusing to sacrifice parts of herself as she grows from a girl to a woman. Hermione never makes Ron "feel better" by pretending to be less than she is; she always preserves who she is and waits for Ron to catch up. In general, Rowling regards her as a heroine, but isn't sexy nor entirely sexless, but a "real girl."
</p><p>Rowling admitted in an interview conducted by Emma Watson for the magazine <i>Wonderland</i> in February of 2014 that, with hindsight, she initially had some second thoughts on the suitability of Ron as a partner for Hermione and believes that in some ways, Harry might have made a better romantic partner for her:
</p>
<dl><dd><i>"I wrote the Hermione-Ron relationship as a form of wish fulfilment. That's how it was conceived, really. For reasons that have very little to do with literature and far more to do with me clinging to the plot as I first imagined it, Hermione [ended up] with Ron."</i></dd></dl>
<p>She went on to say that she found the attraction itself plausible, but that the combative side of it might cause problems in an adult relationship as there was too much fundamental incompatibility. However, according to Rowling, they could "probably be alright" with a bit of marriage counselling, as Ron needed to work on his self-esteem issues while Hermione needed to learn to be less critical. She concluded with the statement that just like herself, the uptight Hermione had a real weakness for a funny man. Ultimately, Rowling stated she had no regrets putting them together and stated the two balanced each other out and truly love one another.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
